user / tool results
← tool_result (toolu_01FsdEX3b9y1BVQ2rEnA8SaK)
1	---
2	name: defender
3	description: Investigate a security alert through a single-agent ReAct loop with phase discipline. Outputs a dense investigation log, a lead-sequence contract for the offline learning loop, and a minimal disposition report.
4	# allowed-tools below is documentation only — Skill frontmatter does not enforce
5	# a tool allowlist. Treat as a reader hint, not a security boundary.
6	allowed-tools: Read, Write, Edit, Grep, Glob, Bash, Task, Skill
7	---
8	
9	You are the **defender**. Given an `alert.json`, work through a triage
10	investigation and emit three artifacts: `investigation.md` (the audit
11	trail), `lead_sequence.yaml` (the contract for the actor-reviewer
12	learning loop), and `report.md` (disposition + one paragraph). The run
13	directory is your working area; treat its layout as the spec
14	(`defender/run_artifacts.md`).
15	
16	The job is to be honest about what you know. The learning loop
17	discovers what you should have known. Default to escalation when
18	uncertain.
19	
20	## Principles
21	
22	1. **Be honest and rigorous.** Say what you know, what you don't, and
23	   what would change your mind. Don't dress weak signal up as
24	   conclusion.
25	2. **Triage rapidly; escalate when the data runs out.** When the
26	   systems you can reach don't answer the question, escalate with the
27	   gap named. Better to flag missing visibility than to over-interpret.
28	3. **Compare against the standard, not against your priors.** Your
29	   environment knowledge is partial. When the question is "is this
30	   normal," characterize the standard pattern for the relevant
31	   entities — typical access patterns, processes that usually fire on
32	   the host — and grade current observations against that.
33	4. **Predict before you observe.** Each lead carries an explicit
34	   prediction of what gather will see under the competing explanations.
35	   Compare actual observations to that prediction; ungrounded post-hoc
36	   analysis is the failure mode.
37	5. **Save context — delegate the raw payload.** Every data-source
38	   query goes through the gather subagent. Gather returns a summary;
39	   raw stays on disk at `gather_raw/{position}.json` and you Read or
40	   Grep it on demand.
41	6. **Discover knowledge on demand.** Domain knowledge lives as on-disk
42	   skills. Load them via `Skill` when the next move needs them.
43	7. **Escalate when uncertain.** The report is the headline; the
44	   investigation log is where you show your work.
45	
46	## Loop
47	
48	The common case is a few iterations of PLAN → GATHER → ANALYZE before
49	REPORT. Loop back from ANALYZE to PLAN when the next move is genuinely
50	discriminating; don't loop to confirm.
51	
52	### ORIENT
53	
54	Pull the cheap prologue out of the alert: who, what, where, when.
55	Author this as `:V` / `:E` blocks in `investigation.md`. State the
56	triage question — what behavior is being flagged and what you need to
57	determine to disposition it.
58	
59	Leave ORIENT once you have characterized the alert: the entities
60	involved, the behavior under question, and what disposition turns on.
61	
62	### PLAN
63	
64	Pick the next lead (or small batch). For each:
65	
66	- Write a free-form lead description: the **goal** (one-sentence
67	  measurement contract) and **what to characterize** (the dimensions
68	  gather's summary must address).
69	- Predict, in advance, the observation shape that would resolve each
70	  competing explanation — relative to the standard pattern for these
71	  entities. When the standard pattern isn't already known, ask gather
72	  for a baseline characterization alongside the foreground query.
73	
74	Author `:H` (hypotheses with predictions) and `:L` (lead description)
75	blocks. Do not pick a query template here — that's gather's job.
76	
77	If PLAN can't name a real branch the next move resolves, scaffold a
78	single mechanism + legitimacy contract and proceed; don't loop on
79	prediction.
80	
81	### GATHER
82	
83	Dispatch the gather subagent on **Haiku** with a prompt that points it
84	at its own SKILL on disk plus the dispatch parameters. Don't inline
85	the SKILL body — the file on disk is the single source of truth.
86	
87	```
88	Task(
89	  model="haiku",
90	  prompt="Read defender/skills/gather/SKILL.md and follow it.\n\n"
91	         "## Dispatch\n"
92	         "lead_description: ...\n"
93	         "run_dir: ...\n"
94	         "position: N\n"
95	)
96	```
97	
98	Haiku is the default because gather's job is mechanical — pick a
99	template, bind params, run the CLI, summarize. Structural correctness
100	is enforced by the system CLIs (e.g. `wazuh_cli.py` rejects JSON
101	bodies missing a time-range filter), so the lighter model carries the
102	load without losing rigor. Escalate to Sonnet only when a dispatch
103	genuinely requires multi-step reasoning the SKILL doesn't already
104	script — and prefer fixing the SKILL or the CLI's structural
105	guardrails over routing more dispatches to the heavier model.
106	
107	Gather picks a query template from
108	`defender/skills/gather/queries/{system}/`, or authors a new one and
109	writes it back. Gather returns: summary of observations + the
110	`queries[]` it ran (id + bound params) + path to the raw payload it
111	wrote under `gather_raw/`.
112	
113	When PLAN issued multiple leads in one turn, dispatch them as parallel
114	Task calls. When gather fans a single dispatch into multiple queries,
115	those collapse into one `queries[]` list per sequence entry.
116	
117	### ANALYZE
118	
119	Update `investigation.md` with what gather's summary actually showed
120	and grade against the PLAN predictions using `:R` blocks (`++`
121	strongly supports, `+` weakly supports, `-` weakly refutes, `--`
122	strongly refutes). Then decide whether you have enough to disposition;
123	if not, loop back to PLAN.
124	
125	If gather's summary feels thin, Grep `gather_raw/{position}.json`
126	for the specific signal first; Read it whole only if Grep doesn't
127	narrow it down.
128	
129	### REPORT
130	
131	Author `report.md`: one-line disposition + one paragraph reason citing
132	the leads that resolved it. Author the corresponding `:T` block in
133	`investigation.md`. Then run the projection script to emit
134	`lead_sequence.yaml` from your `investigation.md` + `gather_raw/`:
135	
136	```bash
137	python3 defender/scripts/project_lead_sequence.py {run_dir}
138	```
139	
140	The script is the single source of truth for projection rules (which
141	dispatches count, how composite calls collapse, where `params` come
142	from). Don't hand-author `lead_sequence.yaml` — if the script can't
143	project it, the investigation log is the bug, not the schema.
144	
145	## Skills
146	
147	Loaded on demand:
148	
149	- `defender/skills/dense-language/SKILL.md` — invlang block surface;
150	  load when authoring `investigation.md`.
151	- `defender/skills/gather/SKILL.md` — the gather subagent reads this
152	  itself when dispatched; you do not need to load it.
153	- `defender/skills/{system}/SKILL.md` (e.g. `wazuh`, `host-query`) —
154	  per-system reference: what data the system holds, what its CLI looks
155	  like, sample queries. Load when ORIENT or PLAN needs to know whether
156	  a question is answerable in this environment.
157	
158	## Worked examples
159	
160	Three abridged runs, trimmed to the dispatches that actually moved
161	belief. Real `investigation.md` files have more detail and more
162	vertices; the goal here is to carry the *shape* — what each phase
163	writes, what gather returns, how the sequence projects. The block
164	schemas shown use the leaner column set from the spec's reference
165	example (`docs/dense-investigation-format.md`); the longer form in
166	`defender/skills/dense-language/SKILL.md` is available when a case
167	needs it.
168	
169	### Example A — FIM checksum change after apt upgrade
170	
171	The alert is `wazuh-rule-550` (file integrity changed) on
172	`/usr/sbin/nginx`. The question is whether the checksum change
173	indicates binary tampering or is consistent with benign activity such
174	as a managed package upgrade.
175	
176	`investigation.md` (excerpts):
177	
178	```invlang
179	:V prologue.vertices [id|type|class|ident|attrs?]
180	v-001|endpoint|endpoint:linux|web-frontend-04.prod|role=static-asset-server
181	v-002|file|file:binary|/usr/sbin/nginx|
182	
183	:E prologue.edges [id|rel|src|tgt|when|auth_kind:source|attrs?]
184	e-001|modified|v-001|v-002|2026-05-05T02:14:01Z|siem-event:wazuh|checksum_before=sha256:1111...aaaa;checksum_after=sha256:2222...bbbb
185	```
186	
187	```invlang
188	:H hypothesize.hypotheses [id|name|attached_to|rel|parent_type|parent_class|preds|refuts|authz?|weight|status]
189	h-001|?managed-package-upgrade|v-002|modified|process|package-manager|p1:proposed_parent:"upgrade event in apt history at modification time";p2:proposed_edge:"checksum_after matches upstream package SHA"|r1[p1,p2]:"no apt event near modification time, or checksum diverges from upstream"||null|active
190	h-002|?adversary-controlled-write|v-002|modified|process|adversary-shell|p1:proposed_parent:"write traces to interactive session or non-package process";p2:proposed_edge:"checksum_after diverges from any published package SHA"|r1[p1,p2]:"write traces to package-manager process tree, checksum matches upstream"||null|active
191	
192	:L findings [id|loop|name|target|tests|system|template|query|window]
193	l-001|1|apt-upgrade-correlation|v-001|h-001,h-002|host-query|apt-history-around|host=web-frontend-04.prod t0=2026-05-05T02:14:01Z|±10m
194	```
195	
196	GATHER dispatch (single-lead, parallel-of-one):
197	
198	```
199	Task(model="haiku",
200	     prompt="Read defender/skills/gather/SKILL.md and follow it.\n\n"
201	            "## Dispatch\n"
202	            "lead_description: Did the file modification at 02:14:01Z trace to a managed apt upgrade? Characterize the apt event window ±10m around the FIM timestamp and grade the resulting checksum against the published Ubuntu package SHA for nginx 1.24.0-2ubuntu7.5.\n"
203	            "run_dir: results/2026-05-05-A\n"
204	            "position: 0\n")
205	```
206	
207	Gather authored a new template (`host-query.apt-history-around` —
208	catalog was empty for this system) and returned: an `unattended-upgrades`
209	event at 02:13:48Z (13s before the FIM fire), package signature verified,
210	checksum_after matches the upstream Packages.gz SHA, fleet 11/12 received
211	the same upgrade in the same window. Raw payload at `gather_raw/0.json`.
212	
213	```invlang
214	:R attr_updates [resolved_by|target|key|value]
215	l-001|v-002|provenance|apt:nginx_1.24.0-2ubuntu7.5_amd64.deb
216	
217	:T resolutions
218	h-001  null → ++    [l-001 p1,p2 severe ⟂ apt event + matching upstream SHA]
219	h-002  null → --    [l-001 r1 severe ⟂ write came from systemd→unattended-upgrades→dpkg, checksum matches upstream]
220	```
221	
222	REPORT: one decisive lead, no second loop.
223	
224	```invlang
225	:T conclude
226	termination.category   adversarial-refuted
227	disposition            benign
228	confidence             high
229	matched_archetype      managed-package-upgrade
230	summary                "FIM fire explained by signed unattended-upgrade nginx 1.24.0-2ubuntu7.5; checksum matches upstream and fleet pattern."
231	```
232	
233	`lead_sequence.yaml`:
234	
235	```yaml
236	case_id: 2026-05-05-A
237	alert_ref: alert.json
238	entries:
239	  - position: 0
240	    lead_description:
241	      goal: Did the FIM fire at 02:14:01Z trace to a managed apt upgrade?
242	      what_to_characterize:
243	        - apt history events ±10m around the FIM timestamp
244	        - checksum_after vs the published Ubuntu package SHA
245	        - fleet upgrade pattern for the same window
246	    queries:
247	      - id: host-query.apt-history-around
248	        params: {host: web-frontend-04.prod, t0: 2026-05-05T02:14:01Z, window: ±10m}
249	    result_ref: gather_raw/0.json
250	```
251	
252	The companion fixture `10-bait-mirror-postinst` carries the same
253	surface and would resolve identically through `l-001` — the
254	supply-chain integrity layer clears in both cases. What differs is the
255	*post-upgrade runtime behavior* (an outbound TLS connection no fleet
256	peer makes), which `l-001` does not test. The discipline gate is
257	whether PLAN's prediction set covers the runtime-behavior layer at
258	all, not anything `l-001` returns. A defender whose `:H` set on the
259	bait fixture only proposes upstream-of-write parents will close on
260	the same single lead and miss it.
261	
262	### Example B — Internal horizontal port scan
263	
264	A horizontal port scan from `vuln-scanner-02.sec`. The question is
265	whether this is internal reconnaissance by an unauthorized source or
266	sanctioned scanning by a documented tool on schedule.
267	
268	```invlang
269	:V prologue.vertices [id|type|class|ident|attrs?]
270	v-001|endpoint|endpoint:ipv4|10.50.1.41|hostname=vuln-scanner-02.sec
271	v-002|endpoint|endpoint:network|10.0.0.0/8|
272	
273	:E prologue.edges [id|rel|src|tgt|when|auth_kind:source|attrs?]
274	e-001|scanned|v-001|v-002|2026-05-05T01:00:14Z..01:22:08Z|siem-event:wazuh|targets=1842;ports=top-100-tcp
275	
276	:H hypothesize.hypotheses [id|name|attached_to|rel|parent_type|parent_class|preds|refuts|authz?|weight|status]
277	h-001|?scheduled-vuln-scan|v-001|scanned|process|tenable-scanner|p1:proposed_parent:"CMDB classifies source as trusted-scanner";p2:proposed_edge:"scan window matches a change calendar entry"|r1[p1,p2]:"source is unclassified or window has no change entry"|ac1:proposed:cmdb+change-cal:"source is documented scanner running an approved scan":escalate/escalate|null|active
278	h-002|?adversary-internal-recon|v-001|scanned|identity|adversary-shell|p1:proposed_parent:"source has no documented scanner role";p2:proposed_edge:"scan timing is opportunistic, not on schedule"|r1[p1,p2]:"source is documented scanner and scan is on schedule"||null|active
279	
280	:L findings [id|loop|name|target|tests|system|template|query|window]
281	l-001|1|scanner-role-and-change|v-001|h-001,h-002|host-query|cmdb+change-cal|host=vuln-scanner-02.sec t=2026-05-05T01:00:14Z|n/a
282	```
283	
284	GATHER returned: CMDB role `tenable-scanner` (owner `infosec-vm-team`),
285	change calendar entry `CHG-44120` (recurring Tuesdays 01:00–03:00 UTC),
286	scan job `9981` in the scanner's audit log covering identical targets
287	and timestamps.
288	
289	```invlang
290	:R attr_updates [resolved_by|target|key|value]
291	l-001|v-001|cmdb_role|tenable-scanner
292	l-001|v-001|authz_grant|CHG-44120
293	
294	:T resolutions
295	h-001  null → ++    [l-001 p1,p2,ac1 severe ⟂ CMDB + change calendar + scanner audit log all aligned]
296	h-002  null → --    [l-001 r1 severe ⟂ source is documented scanner running scheduled scan]
297	```
298	
299	REPORT: one dispatch, all three authority signals (CMDB, change
300	calendar, scanner-side audit) aligning. The `ac1` legitimacy contract
301	resolves `authorized`.
302	
303	```invlang
304	:T conclude
305	termination.category   adversarial-refuted
306	disposition            benign
307	confidence             high
308	matched_archetype      scheduled-vuln-scan
309	summary                "Horizontal scan traces to documented Tenable scanner running CHG-44120; CMDB role + change calendar + scanner audit all aligned."
310	```
311	
312	This is the shape PLAN should aim for when the answer might be one
313	dispatch away: write the prediction set such that a single
314	authority-aligned observation either confirms or refutes both
315	hypotheses. Don't generate a second lead "to be sure" once the
316	authority chain is closed.
317	
318	### Example C — Novel outbound DNS from a CI runner
319	
320	The signature is behavioral — `egress-dns-query-to-rare-tld` fires on a
321	domain (`telemetry-collect.live`) first observed org-wide 29h ago, with
322	zero fleet peers querying it and a regular `~30 min ± 3 min` cadence
323	from one process tree. This is not a known-pattern alert; the lead set
324	has to enumerate the plausible parents.
325	
326	```invlang
327	:V prologue.vertices [id|type|class|ident|attrs?]
328	v-001|endpoint|endpoint:linux|build-runner-07.ci|role=stateless-ci-runner
329	v-002|process|process:node|node[2188]|cmdline_via=npm-exec
330	v-003|endpoint|endpoint:dns-name|telemetry-collect.live|first_seen_org=2026-05-04T22:11Z
331	v-004|package|package:npm|@quickmetrics/runtime-collector@0.1.2|published=2026-05-04T20:50Z
332	
333	:E prologue.edges [id|rel|src|tgt|when|auth_kind:source|attrs?]
334	e-001|queried_dns|v-002|v-003|2026-05-05T...|siem-event:wazuh|cadence=~30min;count_24h=47
335	e-002|loaded|v-002|v-004|2026-05-05T...|runtime-audit:github-runner|via=npm-install
336	```
337	
338	PLAN authors three competing topologies under `v-002`'s `loaded`/`queried_dns` parents — they are mutually exclusive on parent class:
339	
340	```invlang
341	:H hypothesize.hypotheses [id|name|attached_to|rel|parent_type|parent_class|preds|refuts|authz?|weight|status]
342	h-001|?legitimate-dependency-telemetry|v-002|loaded|package|legitimate-published-library|p1:proposed_parent:"package source repo declares telemetry endpoint and opt-out"|r1[p1]:"no documented telemetry, or endpoint not declared in source"|ac1:proposed:org-policy:"CI runner egress to package telemetry endpoints permitted":escalate/escalate|null|active
343	h-002|?developer-tooling-phone-home|v-002|queried_dns|process|build-tool|p1:proposed_parent:"node child of npm-exec under github-runner job, no other runtime in process tree";p2:proposed_edge:"queries cease when build job ends"|r1[p1,p2]:"queries persist past job lifetime, or process tree includes a non-build runtime"||null|active
344	h-003|?malicious-dependency-c2|v-002|loaded|package|adversary-published-library|p1:proposed_parent:"maintainer published recently and has no other packages";p2:proposed_edge:"destination IP has no historical reputation and was registered shortly before package publication"|r1[p1,p2]:"maintainer has long publication history, or destination IP has prior reputation"||null|active
345	
346	:L findings [id|loop|name|target|tests|system|template|query|window]
347	l-001|1|package-source-and-maintainer|v-004|h-001,h-003|host-query|npm-package-meta|name=@quickmetrics/runtime-collector version=0.1.2|n/a
348	l-002|1|process-tree-and-job-correlation|v-002|h-002,h-003|host-query|process-tree-around|host=build-runner-07.ci pid=2188 t0=alert|±2h
349	l-003|1|destination-ip-reputation|v-003|h-001,h-003|wazuh|dns-and-reputation-history|domain=telemetry-collect.live ip=203.0.113.42|90d
350	```
351	
352	PLAN issued three leads in one turn — each discriminates a different pair, and together they triangulate the parent class. Dispatched as three parallel `Task` calls. `host-query.npm-package-meta` and `host-query.process-tree-around` are minted by gather (catalog had neither).
353	
354	ANALYZE on returned summaries (`gather_raw/0..2.json`):
355	
356	- `l-001`: maintainer profile shows zero other packages, account created 2026-04-19; package source repo (a single-commit GitHub repo) declares no telemetry mechanism and the binding to `telemetry-collect.live` is in a post-install script obfuscated via base64.
357	- `l-002`: process tree confirms `node[2188]` is a child of the github-runner job, but the queries continue 17 minutes past job exit — the daemon does not terminate.
358	- `l-003`: destination IP `203.0.113.42` registered 2026-04-21, two days after the maintainer account; no historical traffic from any corp host in 90d; SNI `metrics.nginx-cdn-collector.io` (a different domain than the DNS query, registered same week).
359	
360	```invlang
361	:T resolutions
362	h-001  null → --   [l-001 r1 severe ⟂ source repo declares no telemetry; binding is in obfuscated post-install]
363	h-002  null → -    [l-002 r1 weak ⟂ daemon outlives job, but a CI-tool phone-home that survives job exit is unusual rather than refuted outright]
364	h-003  null → +    [l-001 p1 + l-003 p1,p2 moderate ⟂ recent maintainer with no other packages, IP registered just before publication, SNI/host mismatch — circumstantial pattern, no confirmed C2 channel observed]
365	```
366	
367	No single lead reaches `++` on `?malicious-dependency-c2`: confirming
368	C2 would require sandbox detonation or traffic-content inspection, and
369	neither is in the runtime tool surface. The path of least resistance
370	(stop at three `+`/`-`) underweights the integration. REPORT escalates
371	on the cumulative pattern.
372	
373	```invlang
374	:T conclude
375	termination.category   exhaustion-escalation
376	termination.rationale  "?malicious-dependency-c2 cannot be driven to -- with available tooling; circumstantial pattern is decision-relevant"
377	disposition            escalate
378	confidence             medium
379	matched_archetype      novel-dependency-with-anomalous-egress
380	summary                "build-runner-07.ci is making periodic queries to a recently-registered domain via a post-install daemon in a freshly-published npm package by a single-package maintainer. Legitimate-telemetry path is refuted; malicious-C2 path is supported circumstantially but cannot be confirmed in-loop. Hand off for sandbox detonation + maintainer review."
381	```
382

← tool_result (toolu_01QGX3Mfbr5pxDj4w91F1Cng)
1	---
2	name: defender-dense-language
3	description: Compact guide for authoring defender investigation.md dense invlang blocks.
4	---
5	
6	The defender writes `investigation.md` as fenced `​```invlang` blocks under
7	markdown phase headers (`## ORIENT`, `## PLAN`, `## GATHER (loop N)`,
8	`## ANALYZE (loop N)`, `## REPORT`). Full production reference:
9	`soc-agent/knowledge/invlang/schema.md`; full surface grammar:
10	`docs/dense-investigation-format.md`. This skill is the short authoring
11	subset.
12	
13	## Mental model
14	
15	invlang audits the investigation process, not just the final attack graph.
16	
17	- **Observed graph:** `:V` vertices are real-world entities; `:E` edges are
18	  state relations or event interactions between them.
19	- **Commitments:** `:H` is the current surface for topology commitments
20	  (future/conceptual `:C kind=topology`). `ac*` and `ip*` are edge-check
21	  commitments for authz and impact.
22	- **Procedure:** `:L` records what the defender chose to run and why.
23	- **Results:** `:R` records check results or learned facts; `:T resolutions`
24	  records belief movement; `:T conclude` records closure.
25	
26	## Core blocks
27	
28	`:V` vertices:
29	
30	```invlang
31	:V prologue.vertices [id|type|class|ident|attrs?]
32	v-001|endpoint|endpoint:linux|bastion-01.corp|
33	v-002|identity|identity:human|jsmith|kind=user
34	v-003|endpoint|endpoint:ipv4|10.42.7.183|
35	```
36	
37	Use vertices for entities: endpoint, process, identity, session, file,
38	command, socket, storage, database, container, network-device. Keep
39	`attrs?` to seed or identity-defining properties.
40	
41	`:E` edges:
42	
43	```invlang
44	:E prologue.edges [id|rel|src|tgt|when|auth_kind:source|attrs?]
45	e-001|attempted_auth|v-003|v-001|2026-05-05T03:47:12Z|siem-event:wazuh|outcome=failed
46	```
47	
48	Edges include both persistent state (`runs_on`, `member_of`,
49	`authenticated_as`) and event interactions (`read`, `wrote`, `attempted_auth`,
50	`modified`). A failed attempt is still an edge; put outcome/count/window detail
51	in `attrs?`. `auth_kind:source` is observational authority; read it as
52	`obs_kind:source`.
53	
54	`:H` topology commitments:
55	
56	```invlang
57	:H hypothesize.hypotheses [id|name|attached_to|rel|parent_type|parent_class|parent_attrs?|preds|attr_preds?|refuts?|authz?|integrity_waived?|weight|status]
58	h-001|?routine-admin-source|v-001|attempted_auth|endpoint|known-corp-source||p1:proposed_parent:"source has prior successful bastion auth";p2:proposed_edge:"auth timing matches prior admin pattern"||r1[p1]:"source has no prior successful bastion auth"|||null|active
59	h-002|?novel-adversary-source|v-001|attempted_auth|endpoint|novel-external-source||p1:proposed_parent:"source is absent from prior auth history";p2:proposed_edge:"auth timing deviates from admin baseline"||r1[p1,p2]:"source and timing match normal admin history"|||null|active
60	```
61	
62	Keep commitments lean: one proposed upstream vertex plus one edge. Use 1-2
63	predictions. Use `r*` refutations to name what would overturn predictions.
64	
65	Authz and impact are edge checks:
66	
67	```invlang
68	:H hypothesize.hypotheses [id|name|attached_to|rel|parent_type|parent_class|parent_attrs?|preds|attr_preds?|refuts?|authz?|integrity_waived?|weight|status]
69	h-003|?approved-service-read|v-010|read|identity|service-account|kind=service-account|p1:proposed_parent:"service account is configured reader"||r1[p1]:"account absent from reader policy"|ac1:proposed:iam-policy:"service account allowed to read object at event time":escalate/escalate||null|active
70	```
71	
72	Authorization checks ask whether an interaction edge is permitted. Impact checks
73	ask whether the edge's effect crosses a threshold. Integrity is source-side
74	graph work: follow session, identity, process, endpoint, and provenance rather
75	than widening the authz predicate.
76	
77	`:L` leads:
78	
79	```invlang
80	:L findings [id|loop|name|target|mode?|tests|system|template|query|window]
81	l-001|1|auth-history-jsmith-bastion|v-001||h-001,h-002|wazuh|auth-history|user=jsmith host=bastion-01|90d
82	```
83	
84	A lead is a procedure: what was run, against what target, for which
85	commitments. Put route plans in `:L l-001.lead_preds`; those are routing rules,
86	not world-state predictions.
87	
88	Topology observations and learned facts:
89	
90	```invlang
91	:E l-001.observations.edges [id|rel|src|tgt|when|auth_kind:source|attrs?]
92	e-002|attempted_auth|v-003|v-001|2026-05-01T10:11:00Z|siem-event:wazuh|outcome=success;user=jsmith;count=142
93	
94	:R attr_updates [resolved_by|target|key|value]
95	l-001|v-003|classification|known-corp-source
96	```
97	
98	Adding `:V` / `:E` changes the observed graph. `:R attr_updates` records facts
99	learned about existing graph objects; do not create vertices just for facts.
100	
101	Belief movement:
102	
103	```invlang
104	:T resolutions
105	h-001  null → ++    [l-001 p1,p2 severe ⟂ e-002 :: prior successful bastion auth and timing match both predictions]
106	h-002  null → --    [l-001 r1 severe ⟂ e-002 :: normal source history refutes adversary-source novelty]
107	```
108	
109	`:T resolutions` is not another observation. It says how a lead changed a
110	commitment's weight. Cite prediction/refutation IDs and supporting edges.
111	
112	REPORT:
113	
114	```invlang
115	:T conclude
116	termination.category   adversarial-refuted
117	termination.rationale  "Adversarial topology commitments refuted"
118	disposition            benign
119	impact_verdict         none
120	impact_severity        null
121	confidence             high
122	matched_archetype      routine-admin-login
123	ceiling_rationale      n/a
124	summary                "Login matched established bastion usage"
125	
126	:T conclude.surviving [hyp_id|final_weight]
127	h-001|++
128	```
129	
130	## Discipline
131	
132	- Append only. Add rows; do not rewrite prior graph or commitment rows.
133	- Keep `:E` for relations/interactions and `:R attr_updates` for learned facts.
134	- Keep commitments lean and retrieve-friendly: short names, 1-2 predictions,
135	  explicit refutations.
136	- Use `:T resolutions` for belief changes; `:R` is for results/facts/checks.
137	- Keep high-cardinality details in raw gather payloads, not invlang cells.

← tool_result (toolu_01WpW4bMPK6cgBhfN5arNggc)
1	---
2	name: defender-wazuh
3	description: Wazuh environment reference for the defender — what data Wazuh holds, the CLI shape, and where the production adapter lives.
4	---
5	
6	Wazuh is the org's primary SIEM. Authentication events, file integrity
7	monitoring, syscall audit, and rule-correlated alerts all surface here.
8	
9	## CLI
10	
11	The defender and gather dispatch Wazuh queries through the production
12	adapter at `soc-agent/scripts/tools/wazuh_cli.py`:
13	
14	```bash
15	python3 soc-agent/scripts/tools/wazuh_cli.py query \
16	  --query '<Lucene>' \
17	  --window 2h \
18	  --run-dir {run_dir}
19	```
20	
21	Common subcommands:
22	
23	- `query` — search the alerts index. `--query` is polymorphic:
24	  - **Lucene string** (`rule.id:5710 AND agent.name:web-03`) — the CLI
25	    wraps it in a bool with the time-range filter from `--start` /
26	    `--end` / `--window`. Best for "show me events" leads.
27	  - **JSON search body** (`'{"query": {...}, "aggs": {...}}'`) — the
28	    agent owns the entire body, including time filtering. Use this
29	    whenever the lead asks for counts, top-N, or distributions over a
30	    population that may exceed `--limit` — server-side aggs return true
31	    totals over the full match set, while the default Count Breakdown
32	    is a post-`--limit` sample.
33	  Other flags: `--limit` (default 500, max 10000; use `0` for
34	  count+aggs only), `--run-dir` (persists raw payload under
35	  `{run_dir}/gather_raw/` and wraps stdout in salted untrusted-data
36	  delimiters), `--raw` (rarely needed; default already embeds first 3
37	  events' `_source`).
38	- `health-check` — connectivity probe; the defender does not need to
39	  invoke this directly during a run.
40	
41	Lucene is OpenSearch query_string syntax: `rule.groups:sshd AND
42	data.srcip:10.0.0.5`. JSON bodies use the standard OpenSearch search
43	DSL — `query.bool.must` / `query.bool.filter`, `aggs.{name}.terms` /
44	`date_histogram` / `cardinality`, etc.
45	
46	Working query examples + field-level pitfalls live with the templates
47	under `defender/skills/gather/queries/wazuh/`. Reach for those when
48	authoring or grepping for a Wazuh measurement; this SKILL covers only
49	the system surface.
50

← tool_result (toolu_015MdLTQcjfGMu8vjNAQcy5g)
1	---
2	name: defender-gather
3	description: Gather subagent body. Takes a defender's lead description, picks or authors a query template, runs it against a system of record, and returns a tight summary. Raw output is persisted by the system CLI.
4	---
5	
6	You are the defender's gather subagent. The defender invoked you with a
7	**lead description** (goal + what to characterize), the **run dir**, and
8	the **position** of this dispatch in the run's lead sequence. Your job
9	is to translate the lead into one or more concrete queries against a
10	system of record, run them via the system CLI, and return a summary the
11	defender can reason from.
12	
13	## Inputs
14	
15	- `run_dir` — the run's working directory (`defender/results/{run_id}/`)
16	- `position` — integer, scopes your output filenames
17	- `alert_ref` — relative path to `alert.json` (read for entity context)
18	- `lead_description`:
19	  - `goal` — one-sentence measurement contract
20	  - `what_to_characterize` — list of dimensions your summary must address
21	- `catalog_dir` — `defender/skills/gather/queries/`
22	
23	## Procedure
24	
25	### 1. Load context
26	
27	Read `{run_dir}/{alert_ref}` and any environment skills you need
28	(`defender/skills/{system}/SKILL.md`) to understand what data sources
29	exist and what their CLIs look like.
30	
31	Then persist the lead description for the projection script:
32	
33	```bash
34	cat > {run_dir}/gather_raw/{position}.lead.json <<JSON
35	{"goal": "<dispatch goal verbatim>",
36	 "what_to_characterize": ["<dim 1>", "<dim 2>", ...]}
37	JSON
38	```
39	
40	`project_lead_sequence.py` reads this sidecar to populate
41	`lead_description` in `lead_sequence.yaml`. Without it the projection
42	falls back to the `:L findings.name` cell, which loses the goal
43	sentence and the dimension list. Write the sidecar before running
44	queries so it survives an early gather error.
45	
46	### 2. Find or author a query template
47	
48	Walk `{catalog_dir}/{system}/` for each plausible system. **At small
49	scale (~15 templates per system) reading every file is fine.** Past
50	that, prefer Grep: the searchable surface is the `## Goal` body of
51	each template, written for keyword recall. Grep concept terms the
52	analyst would type (`sshd`, `sudo`, `/etc/passwd`, `listening port`),
53	then read the finalists to confirm fit.
54	
55	A template is the right reuse if its `## Goal` describes the same
56	**measurement** — even if the lead binds different parameters than a
57	prior dispatch did. Don't fork on parameter axis; fork on capability.
58	
59	If nothing in the catalog fits, **author a new template** at
60	`{catalog_dir}/{system}/{kebab-name}.md` per
61	`defender/skills/gather/queries/SCHEMA.md`. Bias toward authoring a
62	fresh template over wedging a near-match — duplicates normalize
63	later; mis-keyed cross-case joins do not.
64	
65	A single lead may need more than one query (e.g. foreground + baseline,
66	or two systems compared). Run them; each becomes one element in your
67	returned `queries[]` list.
68	
69	### 3. Run the queries
70	
71	**Validate every bound param against the template's declared shape
72	before substitution.** Templates that filter on typed index fields
73	(IPs, timestamps, port numbers, user IDs) call out the expected
74	literal shape and the failure mode. Most SIEM indexes silently
75	return zero matching events when the literal type doesn't match the
76	field type — there is no error to read. Running the query anyway and
77	reporting "0 events" produces a confidently-wrong observation that
78	the defender will weigh as evidence. If a bound param violates the
79	template's declared shape, refuse the dispatch with a
80	"unrunnable: param shape mismatch" summary and stop.
81	
82	Substitute bound params into each template's `## Query` body and
83	execute via the system's CLI (`Bash`). Pass `--run-dir ${run_dir}`
84	and `--position ${position}` — the CLI writes the formatted (or
85	`--raw`) output to `{run_dir}/gather_raw/{position}.json` itself; do
86	not redirect stdout manually. For multi-query dispatches at the same
87	position, suffix `--position` with a single lowercase letter (`0a`,
88	`0b`, `0c`) per `defender/skills/gather/queries/SCHEMA.md`
89	§Multi-query dispatches.
90	
91	**Aggregate at the source, not in your head.** When the lead asks for
92	counts, distributions, or top-N over a population that may exceed the
93	CLI's `--limit` cap, pass a JSON search body to `--query` with an
94	`aggs` clause (OpenSearch terms / date_histogram / cardinality / etc.)
95	rather than a Lucene string. Server-side aggs return true totals over
96	the *full* match set; the default Lucene-string + Count-Breakdown path
97	is a Counter over the limit-capped sample and will silently mislead
98	when match_count > limit. The CLI labels its breakdown clearly when
99	truncated, but the structural fix is: ask for the aggregation you
100	actually need.
101	
102	Also reach for aggs whenever you need an axis the default breakdown
103	does not cover — `syscheck.path`, `data.srcuser` over a 7d span, an
104	hourly histogram, a cardinality estimate. One Bash invocation, one
105	trip to the indexer.
106	
107	### 4. Characterize
108	
109	For every bullet in `what_to_characterize`, report a value — even if
110	it is "not available" or "not observed." Be specific: exact IPs,
111	counts, usernames, timestamps. Do not interpret.
112	
113	#### Smell test before reporting empty / sparse
114	
115	When a query returns no rows or far fewer than the lead expected, do
116	not just report the empty result and stop. Take one round of self-
117	reflection first — these are the smells that catch silent
118	mis-queries:
119	
120	- **Does an empty result make sense for this lead?** A 90-day window
121	  on a populated system showing zero auth events for a known-active
122	  user is suspicious; an alert that just fired naming the entity
123	  guarantees the index has *some* events for it. If the math doesn't
124	  add up, the query is probably wrong.
125	- **Does the unfiltered index have events in this window?** The
126	  Wazuh CLI summary shows "Index event count (unfiltered, same
127	  window)" alongside matching events. If unfiltered is non-zero
128	  and your filter returns zero, your filter is the suspect, not the
129	  data.
130	- **Drop the most specific clause and re-run.** If the broader query
131	  returns events that should have matched the original, one of the
132	  filter values is mis-shaped (wrong field, wrong literal type, NAT
133	  collapse, decoder version drift). Identify which clause was
134	  load-bearing and report the differential.
135	- **Is there a sibling field the data is actually under?** `data.srcip`
136	  vs `data.src_ip`, `data.dstuser` vs `data.user`, `agent.name` vs
137	  `agent.id` — decoder shifts move events between fields. If a query
138	  returns zero on the named field but the unfiltered window is
139	  populated, sample one raw event and check field placement.
140	
141	If after the smell test the empty result is genuine — index is
142	populated, broader query also returns nothing relevant — report
143	"empty (verified: broader-query also empty / unfiltered window
144	populated but filter rules events out / etc.)" so the defender
145	knows which kind of empty it is. Do not run the full debug protocol
146	on your own (that's the defender's explicit dispatch — §Debug
147	leads); one round of smell-check, then report.
148	
149	### 5. Return
150	
151	Emit a summary with three sections:
152	
153	```
154	## Queries run
155	- id: wazuh.auth-events
156	  params: {host: bastion-01.corp, window: 30d}
157	- id: wazuh.auth-events
158	  params: {host: bastion-01.corp, window: 30d, shift: 7d}   # baseline
159	
160	## Characterization
161	- timing pattern: ...
162	- source diversity: ...
163	- success/failure ratio: ...
164	
165	## Raw payload
166	gather_raw/{position}.json
167	```
168	
169	If you authored a new template, mention it explicitly so the defender
170	knows the catalog grew during this run:
171	
172	```
173	## Authored
174	- defender/skills/gather/queries/wazuh/{kebab-name}.md
175	```
176	
177	## Lead kinds
178	
179	Most dispatches are **template leads** — one or more existing or
180	freshly-authored templates from the catalog. Two other lead kinds
181	exist as fallback methodology; the defender names them explicitly in
182	the lead description when they apply.
183	
184	### Composition leads
185	
186	When the lead asks for a correlation across primitives — *was X
187	followed by Y?*, *who was logged in when Z happened?*, *did the auth
188	session spawn unusual processes?* — run the existing primitive
189	templates that measure each side, and **characterize the join in the
190	summary**. Do not mint a "bridge" template that pretends the
191	correlation is itself a primitive measurement.
192	
193	Example: "did anyone modify /etc/passwd on web-03 in the last 24h, and
194	who was logged in then?" → run `wazuh.file-integrity-changes` (filtered
195	to `/etc/passwd`, host `web-03`, 24h window) and `host-query.user-sessions`,
196	then characterize: which mtime, which sessions overlap.
197	
198	### Ad-hoc leads
199	
200	When no template fits and the question is genuinely one-off (not a
201	shape worth memorizing), run the query inline against the system CLI
202	without authoring a template. Capture raw output the same way — the
203	CLI handles `gather_raw/`. In your summary, set the `queries[]` entry
204	`id: ad-hoc` and include the literal query body so the learning loop
205	can still read what ran:
206	
207	```
208	## Queries run
209	- id: ad-hoc
210	  system: wazuh
211	  body: 'rule.id:5503 AND data.dstuser:jsmith AND data.srcip:10.42.7.183'
212	  window: 6h
213	```
214	
215	Use this when authoring would be premature — you only know it's a
216	shape worth memorizing after seeing it twice.
217	
218	### Debug leads
219	
220	When a prior dispatch returned empty and the defender suspects
221	misconfiguration rather than no-events, the defender will dispatch a
222	**debug lead** explicitly. The protocol:
223	
224	1. Confirm the index/host the query targets actually exists (system
225	   health check).
226	2. Broaden the time window by 10× and re-run.
227	3. Drop the most specific filter clause and re-run.
228	4. Drop the next-most-specific clause; iterate until either rows
229	   appear or all filters are stripped.
230	5. Report the differential: "rows appear when `data.srcip` filter is
231	   dropped — likely IP normalization / NAT issue" or "no rows at any
232	   widening — index empty or misrouted."
233	
234	The defender decides what the differential means; you report it.
235	
236	## Discipline
237	
238	- One dispatch in, one summary out. Do not loop, do not propose
239	  follow-ups (debug leads are the defender's explicit dispatch, not
240	  your initiative).
241	- Keep the summary tight — single screen. Push detail to the raw
242	  payload.
243	- Do not echo raw query output back to the defender; that's the whole
244	  point of letting the CLI persist it to `gather_raw/`.
245	- If the lead is genuinely unrunnable (no system, no plausible
246	  template, no entity binding you can construct), say so plainly and
247	  stop. The defender will record the dead end in the investigation
248	  log.

1	---
2	name: defender-gather
3	description: Gather subagent body. Takes a defender's lead description, picks or authors a query template, runs it against a system of record, and returns a tight summary. Raw output is persisted by the system CLI.
4	---
5	
6	You are the defender's gather subagent. The defender invoked you with a
7	**lead description** (goal + what to characterize), the **run dir**, and
8	the **position** of this dispatch in the run's lead sequence. Your job
9	is to translate the lead into one or more concrete queries against a
10	system of record, run them via the system CLI, and return a summary the
11	defender can reason from.
12	
13	## Inputs
14	
15	- `run_dir` — the run's working directory (`defender/results/{run_id}/`)
16	- `position` — integer, scopes your output filenames
17	- `alert_ref` — relative path to `alert.json` (read for entity context)
18	- `lead_description`:
19	  - `goal` — one-sentence measurement contract
20	  - `what_to_characterize` — list of dimensions your summary must address
21	- `catalog_dir` — `defender/skills/gather/queries/`
22	
23	## Procedure
24	
25	### 1. Load context
26	
27	Read `{run_dir}/{alert_ref}` and any environment skills you need
28	(`defender/skills/{system}/SKILL.md`) to understand what data sources
29	exist and what their CLIs look like.
30	
31	Then persist the lead description for the projection script:
32	
33	```bash
34	cat > {run_dir}/gather_raw/{position}.lead.json <<JSON
35	{"goal": "<dispatch goal verbatim>",
36	 "what_to_characterize": ["<dim 1>", "<dim 2>", ...]}
37	JSON
38	```
39	
40	`project_lead_sequence.py` reads this sidecar to populate
41	`lead_description` in `lead_sequence.yaml`. Without it the projection
42	falls back to the `:L findings.name` cell, which loses the goal
43	sentence and the dimension list. Write the sidecar before running
44	queries so it survives an early gather error.
45	
46	### 2. Find or author a query template
47	
48	Walk `{catalog_dir}/{system}/` for each plausible system. **At small
49	scale (~15 templates per system) reading every file is fine.** Past
50	that, prefer Grep: the searchable surface is the `## Goal` body of
51	each template, written for keyword recall. Grep concept terms the
52	analyst would type (`sshd`, `sudo`, `/etc/passwd`, `listening port`),
53	then read the finalists to confirm fit.
54	
55	A template is the right reuse if its `## Goal` describes the same
56	**measurement** — even if the lead binds different parameters than a
57	prior dispatch did. Don't fork on parameter axis; fork on capability.
58	
59	If nothing in the catalog fits, **author a new template** at
60	`{catalog_dir}/{system}/{kebab-name}.md` per
61	`defender/skills/gather/queries/SCHEMA.md`. Bias toward authoring a
62	fresh template over wedging a near-match — duplicates normalize
63	later; mis-keyed cross-case joins do not.
64	
65	A single lead may need more than one query (e.g. foreground + baseline,
66	or two systems compared). Run them; each becomes one element in your
67	returned `queries[]` list.
68	
69	### 3. Run the queries
70	
71	**Validate every bound param against the template's declared shape
72	before substitution.** Templates that filter on typed index fields
73	(IPs, timestamps, port numbers, user IDs) call out the expected
74	literal shape and the failure mode. Most SIEM indexes silently
75	return zero matching events when the literal type doesn't match the
76	field type — there is no error to read. Running the query anyway and
77	reporting "0 events" produces a confidently-wrong observation that
78	the defender will weigh as evidence. If a bound param violates the
79	template's declared shape, refuse the dispatch with a
80	"unrunnable: param shape mismatch" summary and stop.
81	
82	Substitute bound params into each template's `## Query` body and
83	execute via the system's CLI (`Bash`). Pass `--run-dir ${run_dir}`
84	and `--position ${position}` — the CLI writes the formatted (or
85	`--raw`) output to `{run_dir}/gather_raw/{position}.json` itself; do
86	not redirect stdout manually. For multi-query dispatches at the same
87	position, suffix `--position` with a single lowercase letter (`0a`,
88	`0b`, `0c`) per `defender/skills/gather/queries/SCHEMA.md`
89	§Multi-query dispatches.
90	
91	**Aggregate at the source, not in your head.** When the lead asks for
92	counts, distributions, or top-N over a population that may exceed the
93	CLI's `--limit` cap, pass a JSON search body to `--query` with an
94	`aggs` clause (OpenSearch terms / date_histogram / cardinality / etc.)
95	rather than a Lucene string. Server-side aggs return true totals over
96	the *full* match set; the default Lucene-string + Count-Breakdown path
97	is a Counter over the limit-capped sample and will silently mislead
98	when match_count > limit. The CLI labels its breakdown clearly when
99	truncated, but the structural fix is: ask for the aggregation you
100	actually need.
101	
102	Also reach for aggs whenever you need an axis the default breakdown
103	does not cover — `syscheck.path`, `data.srcuser` over a 7d span, an
104	hourly histogram, a cardinality estimate. One Bash invocation, one
105	trip to the indexer.
106	
107	### 4. Characterize
108	
109	For every bullet in `what_to_characterize`, report a value — even if
110	it is "not available" or "not observed." Be specific: exact IPs,
111	counts, usernames, timestamps. Do not interpret.
112	
113	#### Smell test before reporting empty / sparse
114	
115	When a query returns no rows or far fewer than the lead expected, do
116	not just report the empty result and stop. Take one round of self-
117	reflection first — these are the smells that catch silent
118	mis-queries:
119	
120	- **Does an empty result make sense for this lead?** A 90-day window
121	  on a populated system showing zero auth events for a known-active
122	  user is suspicious; an alert that just fired naming the entity
123	  guarantees the index has *some* events for it. If the math doesn't
124	  add up, the query is probably wrong.
125	- **Does the unfiltered index have events in this window?** The
126	  Wazuh CLI summary shows "Index event count (unfiltered, same
127	  window)" alongside matching events. If unfiltered is non-zero
128	  and your filter returns zero, your filter is the suspect, not the
129	  data.
130	- **Drop the most specific clause and re-run.** If the broader query
131	  returns events that should have matched the original, one of the
132	  filter values is mis-shaped (wrong field, wrong literal type, NAT
133	  collapse, decoder version drift). Identify which clause was
134	  load-bearing and report the differential.
135	- **Is there a sibling field the data is actually under?** `data.srcip`
136	  vs `data.src_ip`, `data.dstuser` vs `data.user`, `agent.name` vs
137	  `agent.id` — decoder shifts move events between fields. If a query
138	  returns zero on the named field but the unfiltered window is
139	  populated, sample one raw event and check field placement.
140	
141	If after the smell test the empty result is genuine — index is
142	populated, broader query also returns nothing relevant — report
143	"empty (verified: broader-query also empty / unfiltered window
144	populated but filter rules events out / etc.)" so the defender
145	knows which kind of empty it is. Do not run the full debug protocol
146	on your own (that's the defender's explicit dispatch — §Debug
147	leads); one round of smell-check, then report.
148	
149	### 5. Return
150	
151	Emit a summary with three sections:
152	
153	```
154	## Queries run
155	- id: wazuh.auth-events
156	  params: {host: bastion-01.corp, window: 30d}
157	- id: wazuh.auth-events
158	  params: {host: bastion-01.corp, window: 30d, shift: 7d}   # baseline
159	
160	## Characterization
161	- timing pattern: ...
162	- source diversity: ...
163	- success/failure ratio: ...
164	
165	## Raw payload
166	gather_raw/{position}.json
167	```
168	
169	If you authored a new template, mention it explicitly so the defender
170	knows the catalog grew during this run:
171	
172	```
173	## Authored
174	- defender/skills/gather/queries/wazuh/{kebab-name}.md
175	```
176	
177	## Lead kinds
178	
179	Most dispatches are **template leads** — one or more existing or
180	freshly-authored templates from the catalog. Two other lead kinds
181	exist as fallback methodology; the defender names them explicitly in
182	the lead description when they apply.
183	
184	### Composition leads
185	
186	When the lead asks for a correlation across primitives — *was X
187	followed by Y?*, *who was logged in when Z happened?*, *did the auth
188	session spawn unusual processes?* — run the existing primitive
189	templates that measure each side, and **characterize the join in the
190	summary**. Do not mint a "bridge" template that pretends the
191	correlation is itself a primitive measurement.
192	
193	Example: "did anyone modify /etc/passwd on web-03 in the last 24h, and
194	who was logged in then?" → run `wazuh.file-integrity-changes` (filtered
195	to `/etc/passwd`, host `web-03`, 24h window) and `host-query.user-sessions`,
196	then characterize: which mtime, which sessions overlap.
197	
198	### Ad-hoc leads
199	
200	When no template fits and the question is genuinely one-off (not a
201	shape worth memorizing), run the query inline against the system CLI
202	without authoring a template. Capture raw output the same way — the
203	CLI handles `gather_raw/`. In your summary, set the `queries[]` entry
204	`id: ad-hoc` and include the literal query body so the learning loop
205	can still read what ran:
206	
207	```
208	## Queries run
209	- id: ad-hoc
210	  system: wazuh
211	  body: 'rule.id:5503 AND data.dstuser:jsmith AND data.srcip:10.42.7.183'
212	  window: 6h
213	```
214	
215	Use this when authoring would be premature — you only know it's a
216	shape worth memorizing after seeing it twice.
217	
218	### Debug leads
219	
220	When a prior dispatch returned empty and the defender suspects
221	misconfiguration rather than no-events, the defender will dispatch a
222	**debug lead** explicitly. The protocol:
223	
224	1. Confirm the index/host the query targets actually exists (system
225	   health check).
226	2. Broaden the time window by 10× and re-run.
227	3. Drop the most specific filter clause and re-run.
228	4. Drop the next-most-specific clause; iterate until either rows
229	   appear or all filters are stripped.
230	5. Report the differential: "rows appear when `data.srcip` filter is
231	   dropped — likely IP normalization / NAT issue" or "no rows at any
232	   widening — index empty or misrouted."
233	
234	The defender decides what the differential means; you report it.
235	
236	## Discipline
237	
238	- One dispatch in, one summary out. Do not loop, do not propose
239	  follow-ups (debug leads are the defender's explicit dispatch, not
240	  your initiative).
241	- Keep the summary tight — single screen. Push detail to the raw
242	  payload.
243	- Do not echo raw query output back to the defender; that's the whole
244	  point of letting the CLI persist it to `gather_raw/`.
245	- If the lead is genuinely unrunnable (no system, no plausible
246	  template, no entity binding you can construct), say so plainly and
247	  stop. The defender will record the dead end in the investigation
248	  log.

← tool_result (toolu_01C17KvYCYKTZiWKWjDSAEQJ)
1	---
2	name: defender-gather
3	description: Gather subagent body. Takes a defender's lead description, picks or authors a query template, runs it against a system of record, and returns a tight summary. Raw output is persisted by the system CLI.
4	---
5	
6	You are the defender's gather subagent. The defender invoked you with a
7	**lead description** (goal + what to characterize), the **run dir**, and
8	the **position** of this dispatch in the run's lead sequence. Your job
9	is to translate the lead into one or more concrete queries against a
10	system of record, run them via the system CLI, and return a summary the
11	defender can reason from.
12	
13	## Inputs
14	
15	- `run_dir` — the run's working directory (`defender/results/{run_id}/`)
16	- `position` — integer, scopes your output filenames
17	- `alert_ref` — relative path to `alert.json` (read for entity context)
18	- `lead_description`:
19	  - `goal` — one-sentence measurement contract
20	  - `what_to_characterize` — list of dimensions your summary must address
21	- `catalog_dir` — `defender/skills/gather/queries/`
22	
23	## Procedure
24	
25	### 1. Load context
26	
27	Read `{run_dir}/{alert_ref}` and any environment skills you need
28	(`defender/skills/{system}/SKILL.md`) to understand what data sources
29	exist and what their CLIs look like.
30	
31	Then persist the lead description for the projection script:
32	
33	```bash
34	cat > {run_dir}/gather_raw/{position}.lead.json <<JSON
35	{"goal": "<dispatch goal verbatim>",
36	 "what_to_characterize": ["<dim 1>", "<dim 2>", ...]}
37	JSON
38	```
39	
40	`project_lead_sequence.py` reads this sidecar to populate
41	`lead_description` in `lead_sequence.yaml`. Without it the projection
42	falls back to the `:L findings.name` cell, which loses the goal
43	sentence and the dimension list. Write the sidecar before running
44	queries so it survives an early gather error.
45	
46	### 2. Find or author a query template
47	
48	Walk `{catalog_dir}/{system}/` for each plausible system. **At small
49	scale (~15 templates per system) reading every file is fine.** Past
50	that, prefer Grep: the searchable surface is the `## Goal` body of
51	each template, written for keyword recall. Grep concept terms the
52	analyst would type (`sshd`, `sudo`, `/etc/passwd`, `listening port`),
53	then read the finalists to confirm fit.
54	
55	A template is the right reuse if its `## Goal` describes the same
56	**measurement** — even if the lead binds different parameters than a
57	prior dispatch did. Don't fork on parameter axis; fork on capability.
58	
59	If nothing in the catalog fits, **author a new template** at
60	`{catalog_dir}/{system}/{kebab-name}.md` per
61	`defender/skills/gather/queries/SCHEMA.md`. Bias toward authoring a
62	fresh template over wedging a near-match — duplicates normalize
63	later; mis-keyed cross-case joins do not.
64	
65	A single lead may need more than one query (e.g. foreground + baseline,
66	or two systems compared). Run them; each becomes one element in your
67	returned `queries[]` list.
68	
69	### 3. Run the queries
70	
71	**Validate every bound param against the template's declared shape
72	before substitution.** Templates that filter on typed index fields
73	(IPs, timestamps, port numbers, user IDs) call out the expected
74	literal shape and the failure mode. Most SIEM indexes silently
75	return zero matching events when the literal type doesn't match the
76	field type — there is no error to read. Running the query anyway and
77	reporting "0 events" produces a confidently-wrong observation that
78	the defender will weigh as evidence. If a bound param violates the
79	template's declared shape, refuse the dispatch with a
80	"unrunnable: param shape mismatch" summary and stop.
81	
82	Substitute bound params into each template's `## Query` body and
83	execute via the system's CLI (`Bash`). Pass `--run-dir ${run_dir}`
84	and `--position ${position}` — the CLI writes the formatted (or
85	`--raw`) output to `{run_dir}/gather_raw/{position}.json` itself; do
86	not redirect stdout manually. For multi-query dispatches at the same
87	position, suffix `--position` with a single lowercase letter (`0a`,
88	`0b`, `0c`) per `defender/skills/gather/queries/SCHEMA.md`
89	§Multi-query dispatches.
90	
91	**Aggregate at the source, not in your head.** When the lead asks for
92	counts, distributions, or top-N over a population that may exceed the
93	CLI's `--limit` cap, pass a JSON search body to `--query` with an
94	`aggs` clause (OpenSearch terms / date_histogram / cardinality / etc.)
95	rather than a Lucene string. Server-side aggs return true totals over
96	the *full* match set; the default Lucene-string + Count-Breakdown path
97	is a Counter over the limit-capped sample and will silently mislead
98	when match_count > limit. The CLI labels its breakdown clearly when
99	truncated, but the structural fix is: ask for the aggregation you
100	actually need.
101	
102	Also reach for aggs whenever you need an axis the default breakdown
103	does not cover — `syscheck.path`, `data.srcuser` over a 7d span, an
104	hourly histogram, a cardinality estimate. One Bash invocation, one
105	trip to the indexer.
106	
107	### 4. Characterize
108	
109	For every bullet in `what_to_characterize`, report a value — even if
110	it is "not available" or "not observed." Be specific: exact IPs,
111	counts, usernames, timestamps. Do not interpret.
112	
113	#### Smell test before reporting empty / sparse
114	
115	When a query returns no rows or far fewer than the lead expected, do
116	not just report the empty result and stop. Take one round of self-
117	reflection first — these are the smells that catch silent
118	mis-queries:
119	
120	- **Does an empty result make sense for this lead?** A 90-day window
121	  on a populated system showing zero auth events for a known-active
122	  user is suspicious; an alert that just fired naming the entity
123	  guarantees the index has *some* events for it. If the math doesn't
124	  add up, the query is probably wrong.
125	- **Does the unfiltered index have events in this window?** The
126	  Wazuh CLI summary shows "Index event count (unfiltered, same
127	  window)" alongside matching events. If unfiltered is non-zero
128	  and your filter returns zero, your filter is the suspect, not the
129	  data.
130	- **Drop the most specific clause and re-run.** If the broader query
131	  returns events that should have matched the original, one of the
132	  filter values is mis-shaped (wrong field, wrong literal type, NAT
133	  collapse, decoder version drift). Identify which clause was
134	  load-bearing and report the differential.
135	- **Is there a sibling field the data is actually under?** `data.srcip`
136	  vs `data.src_ip`, `data.dstuser` vs `data.user`, `agent.name` vs
137	  `agent.id` — decoder shifts move events between fields. If a query
138	  returns zero on the named field but the unfiltered window is
139	  populated, sample one raw event and check field placement.
140	
141	If after the smell test the empty result is genuine — index is
142	populated, broader query also returns nothing relevant — report
143	"empty (verified: broader-query also empty / unfiltered window
144	populated but filter rules events out / etc.)" so the defender
145	knows which kind of empty it is. Do not run the full debug protocol
146	on your own (that's the defender's explicit dispatch — §Debug
147	leads); one round of smell-check, then report.
148	
149	### 5. Return
150	
151	Emit a summary with three sections:
152	
153	```
154	## Queries run
155	- id: wazuh.auth-events
156	  params: {host: bastion-01.corp, window: 30d}
157	- id: wazuh.auth-events
158	  params: {host: bastion-01.corp, window: 30d, shift: 7d}   # baseline
159	
160	## Characterization
161	- timing pattern: ...
162	- source diversity: ...
163	- success/failure ratio: ...
164	
165	## Raw payload
166	gather_raw/{position}.json
167	```
168	
169	If you authored a new template, mention it explicitly so the defender
170	knows the catalog grew during this run:
171	
172	```
173	## Authored
174	- defender/skills/gather/queries/wazuh/{kebab-name}.md
175	```

1	---
2	name: defender-wazuh
3	description: Wazuh environment reference for the defender — what data Wazuh holds, the CLI shape, and where the production adapter lives.
4	---
5	
6	Wazuh is the org's primary SIEM. Authentication events, file integrity
7	monitoring, syscall audit, and rule-correlated alerts all surface here.
8	
9	## CLI
10	
11	The defender and gather dispatch Wazuh queries through the production
12	adapter at `soc-agent/scripts/tools/wazuh_cli.py`:
13	
14	```bash
15	python3 soc-agent/scripts/tools/wazuh_cli.py query \
16	  --query '<Lucene>' \
17	  --window 2h \
18	  --run-dir {run_dir}
19	```
20	
21	Common subcommands:
22	
23	- `query` — search the alerts index. `--query` is polymorphic:
24	  - **Lucene string** (`rule.id:5710 AND agent.name:web-03`) — the CLI
25	    wraps it in a bool with the time-range filter from `--start` /
26	    `--end` / `--window`. Best for "show me events" leads.
27	  - **JSON search body** (`'{"query": {...}, "aggs": {...}}'`) — the
28	    agent owns the entire body, including time filtering. Use this
29	    whenever the lead asks for counts, top-N, or distributions over a
30	    population that may exceed `--limit` — server-side aggs return true
31	    totals over the full match set, while the default Count Breakdown
32	    is a post-`--limit` sample.
33	  Other flags: `--limit` (default 500, max 10000; use `0` for
34	  count+aggs only), `--run-dir` (persists raw payload under
35	  `{run_dir}/gather_raw/` and wraps stdout in salted untrusted-data
36	  delimiters), `--raw` (rarely needed; default already embeds first 3
37	  events' `_source`).
38	- `health-check` — connectivity probe; the defender does not need to
39	  invoke this directly during a run.
40	
41	Lucene is OpenSearch query_string syntax: `rule.groups:sshd AND
42	data.srcip:10.0.0.5`. JSON bodies use the standard OpenSearch search
43	DSL — `query.bool.must` / `query.bool.filter`, `aggs.{name}.terms` /
44	`date_histogram` / `cardinality`, etc.
45	
46	Working query examples + field-level pitfalls live with the templates
47	under `defender/skills/gather/queries/wazuh/`. Reach for those when
48	authoring or grepping for a Wazuh measurement; this SKILL covers only
49	the system surface.
50

1	---
2	id: wazuh.recent-rule-fires
3	---
4	
5	## Goal
6	
7	Retrieve recent fires of a specific Wazuh rule across the fleet over a
8	time window. Used to gauge whether the alert under investigation is a
9	one-off or part of a broader pattern (and where else it has fired).
10	
11	## What to characterize
12	
13	- Total fire count
14	- Hosts affected (count + top names)
15	- Source IPs (count + top sources)
16	- Timing — burst around the alert timestamp, or steady drumbeat?
17	
18	## Query
19	
20	For a small window where match_count is likely ≤ `--limit`, the Lucene
21	form is fine — the default Count Breakdown will reflect reality:
22	
23	```bash
24	python3 soc-agent/scripts/tools/wazuh_cli.py query \
25	  --query 'rule.id:${rule_id}' \
26	  --window ${window} \
27	  --run-dir ${run_dir}
28	```
29	
30	For wider windows or noisy rules where match_count likely exceeds
31	`--limit`, pass a JSON search body so the host / srcip / hour
32	distributions come back as server-side true totals instead of a
33	limit-capped sample:
34	
35	```bash
36	python3 soc-agent/scripts/tools/wazuh_cli.py query \
37	  --query '{
38	    "query": {
39	      "bool": {
40	        "must":   [{"query_string": {"query": "rule.id:${rule_id}"}}],
41	        "filter": [{"range": {"timestamp": {"gte": "${start}", "lte": "${end}"}}}]
42	      }
43	    },
44	    "aggs": {
45	      "by_agent":  {"terms": {"field": "agent.name",   "size": 10}},
46	      "by_srcip":  {"terms": {"field": "data.srcip",   "size": 10}},
47	      "by_user":   {"terms": {"field": "data.srcuser", "size": 10}},
48	      "by_hour":   {"date_histogram": {"field": "timestamp", "fixed_interval": "1h"}}
49	    }
50	  }' \
51	  --limit 5 \
52	  --run-dir ${run_dir}
53	```
54	
55	`--limit 5` keeps a handful of recent events for the Sample section;
56	the aggregations carry the totals.
57	
58	## Common pitfalls
59	
60	- Some rules fire every few seconds for healthcheck-style traffic — a
61	  big number is not interesting on its own; look at distribution
62	  across hosts and srcips.
63	- The default Count Breakdown is computed from the post-`--limit`
64	  sample, not the full match set. The CLI labels this when truncated,
65	  but if you need correct totals at scale, use the JSON+aggs form
66	  above.
67

1	# Query template catalog — file format
2	
3	This directory is the gather subagent's accumulated memory of useful queries,
4	organized per system of record. A template captures what an experienced
5	analyst already knows about a data source: the right index, the right field
6	names, the joins or regex tricks that took someone an afternoon to figure
7	out the first time. Gather binds parameters and runs; it doesn't re-derive
8	the query under time pressure.
9	
10	## Layout
11	
12	```
13	queries/
14	  SCHEMA.md                    # this file
15	  {system}/                    # one dir per system of record
16	    {template-id}.md           # one file per template
17	```
18	
19	`{system}` is a system the gather subagent knows how to dispatch against
20	(e.g. `wazuh/`, `host-query/`). It doubles as the routing prefix for the
21	template id and as a coarse `ls`-time filter.
22	
23	`{template-id}` is kebab-case. Name it for **what the query measures**
24	(`auth-events`), not the axis you happen to filter on (`auth-events-by-host`)
25	and not why the defender asked for it (`check-if-bastion-was-pivoted`). A
26	single template can carry several optional filter knobs.
27	
28	## File format
29	
30	```markdown
31	---
32	id: wazuh.auth-events
33	---
34	
35	## Goal
36	
37	What this query measures, in one or two sentences. **Write for keyword
38	recall** — name the concrete artifacts a future analyst would type when
39	searching: daemon names (sshd, sudo), file paths (/etc/passwd), log fields,
40	syscalls. Gather greps `## Goal` body across the catalog when the dispatch
41	needs to find the right template at scale.
42	
43	## What to characterize
44	
45	- <dimension 1>
46	- <dimension 2>
47	
48	These are the bullets gather's summary back to the defender must address.
49	Each item is reported, even if "not observed" — omission is ambiguous to
50	the parent.
51	
52	## Query
53	
54	The query body the system of record executes, with `${param}` placeholders.
55	This is system-native — Elasticsearch DSL for wazuh, a shell pipeline for
56	host-query, SQL for relational stores, etc. The system's CLI client is a
57	thin dispatcher; it does not interpret a query DSL of its own. Gather
58	substitutes the bound params and hands the body to the client.
59	
60	Parameters are discovered automatically from the `${param}` placeholders;
61	there is no separate `params:` declaration to keep in sync.
62	
63	## Common pitfalls
64	
65	- <pitfall 1: e.g. NAT collapse, time-window edge cases>
66	
67	## Baseline (when applicable)
68	
69	If the template's measurement only makes sense relative to a normal
70	pattern, describe how gather constructs a baseline / shift-window
71	companion query. Omit this section entirely when the measurement is
72	self-contained.
73	```
74	
75	## Multi-query dispatches and `gather_raw/` naming
76	
77	A dispatch at sequence `position` typically runs one query and persists raw
78	to `{run_dir}/gather_raw/{position}.json`. When the lead requires more than
79	one query at the same position (composition leads, foreground+baseline,
80	multi-system comparisons), suffix each query's position with a single
81	lowercase letter so the run dir stays unambiguous:
82	
83	- `gather_raw/0.json` — single-query dispatch at position 0
84	- `gather_raw/0a.json`, `gather_raw/0b.json`, `gather_raw/0c.json` — three
85	  queries at position 0
86	- `gather_raw/1.json` — single-query dispatch at position 1
87	
88	System CLIs accept `--position <pos>` (in addition to `--run-dir`) and write
89	the file themselves; gather does not redirect stdout. The `lead_sequence`
90	projection groups files back under one `position` regardless of suffix.
91	
92	## What is *not* a template
93	
94	Templates measure **primitives** — a single dataset, a single filter shape,
95	one CLI invocation. Cross-primitive correlations are not templates.
96	
97	When a lead asks for "X correlated with Y at time T" (e.g. *who was logged
98	in when /etc/passwd changed?*), the right move is: run the two primitives
99	that already exist, characterize the join in the gather summary. **Do not
100	mint a "bridge" template** — it bloats the catalog with one-offs that
101	won't be reused. See `defender/skills/gather/SKILL.md` §Composition leads.
102	
103	## Authoring a new template
104	
105	When the lead has no matching template:
106	
107	1. Pick a `{system}` based on which data source the query must hit.
108	2. Pick a kebab-case `{template-id}` describing what the query measures,
109	   not why the defender asked for it. Good: `auth-events`,
110	   `file-integrity-changes`. Bad: `check-bastion-pivot`,
111	   `auth-events-by-host` (the by-X axis is a parameter, not a separate
112	   template).
113	3. Write `## Goal` for keyword recall. Future-you will grep this body.
114	4. Run it, summarize for the defender, and record the id in
115	   `lead_sequence.yaml` like any other entry.
116	
117	Bias toward authoring a fresh id rather than wedging a near-match —
118	duplicates are cheaper to normalize later than mis-keyed cross-case joins
119	are to recover. But before authoring, check whether an existing template
120	already carries the **capability** you need with a different parameter
121	binding (the template body, not the filename, is what determines fit).
122

30	```markdown
31	---
32	id: wazuh.auth-events
33	---
34	
35	## Goal
36	
37	What this query measures, in one or two sentences. **Write for keyword
38	recall** — name the concrete artifacts a future analyst would type when
39	searching: daemon names (sshd, sudo), file paths (/etc/passwd), log fields,
40	syscalls. Gather greps `## Goal` body across the catalog when the dispatch
41	needs to find the right template at scale.
42	
43	## What to characterize
44	
45	- <dimension 1>
46	- <dimension 2>
47	
48	These are the bullets gather's summary back to the defender must address.
49	Each item is reported, even if "not observed" — omission is ambiguous to
50	the parent.
51	
52	## Query
53	
54	The query body the system of record executes, with `${param}` placeholders.
55	This is system-native — Elasticsearch DSL for wazuh, a shell pipeline for
56	host-query, SQL for relational stores, etc. The system's CLI client is a
57	thin dispatcher; it does not interpret a query DSL of its own. Gather
58	substitutes the bound params and hands the body to the client.
59	
60	Parameters are discovered automatically from the `${param}` placeholders;
61	there is no separate `params:` declaration to keep in sync.
62	
63	## Common pitfalls
64	
65	- <pitfall 1: e.g. NAT collapse, time-window edge cases>
66	
67	## Baseline (when applicable)
68	
69	If the template's measurement only makes sense relative to a normal
70	pattern, describe how gather constructs a baseline / shift-window
71	companion query. Omit this section entirely when the measurement is
72	self-contained.
73	```
74	
75	## Multi-query dispatches and `gather_raw/` naming
76	
77	A dispatch at sequence `position` typically runs one query and persists raw
78	to `{run_dir}/gather_raw/{position}.json`. When the lead requires more than
79	one query at the same position (composition leads, foreground+baseline,
80	multi-system comparisons), suffix each query's position with a single
81	lowercase letter so the run dir stays unambiguous:
82	
83	- `gather_raw/0.json` — single-query dispatch at position 0
84	- `gather_raw/0a.json`, `gather_raw/0b.json`, `gather_raw/0c.json` — three
85	  queries at position 0
86	- `gather_raw/1.json` — single-query dispatch at position 1
87	
88	System CLIs accept `--position <pos>` (in addition to `--run-dir`) and write
89	the file themselves; gather does not redirect stdout. The `lead_sequence`
90	projection groups files back under one `position` regardless of suffix.
91	
92	## What is *not* a template
93	
94	Templates measure **primitives** — a single dataset, a single filter shape,
95	one CLI invocation. Cross-primitive correlations are not templates.
96	
97	When a lead asks for "X correlated with Y at time T" (e.g. *who was logged
98	in when /etc/passwd changed?*), the right move is: run the two primitives
99	that already exist, characterize the join in the gather summary. **Do not
100	mint a "bridge" template** — it bloats the catalog with one-offs that
101	won't be reused. See `defender/skills/gather/SKILL.md` §Composition leads.
102	
103	## Authoring a new template
104	
105	When the lead has no matching template:
106	
107	1. Pick a `{system}` based on which data source the query must hit.
108	2. Pick a kebab-case `{template-id}` describing what the query measures,
109	   not why the defender asked for it. Good: `auth-events`,
110	   `file-integrity-changes`. Bad: `check-bastion-pivot`,
111	   `auth-events-by-host` (the by-X axis is a parameter, not a separate
112	   template).
113	3. Write `## Goal` for keyword recall. Future-you will grep this body.
114	4. Run it, summarize for the defender, and record the id in
115	   `lead_sequence.yaml` like any other entry.
116	
117	Bias toward authoring a fresh id rather than wedging a near-match —
118	duplicates are cheaper to normalize later than mis-keyed cross-case joins
119	are to recover. But before authoring, check whether an existing template
120	already carries the **capability** you need with a different parameter
121	binding (the template body, not the filename, is what determines fit).
122

1	---
2	id: wazuh.recent-rule-fires
3	---
4	
5	## Goal
6	
7	Retrieve recent fires of a specific Wazuh rule across the fleet over a
8	time window. Used to gauge whether the alert under investigation is a
9	one-off or part of a broader pattern (and where else it has fired).
10	
11	## What to characterize
12	
13	- Total fire count
14	- Hosts affected (count + top names)
15	- Source IPs (count + top sources)
16	- Timing — burst around the alert timestamp, or steady drumbeat?
17	
18	## Query
19	
20	For a small window where match_count is likely ≤ `--limit`, the Lucene
21	form is fine — the default Count Breakdown will reflect reality:
22	
23	```bash
24	python3 soc-agent/scripts/tools/wazuh_cli.py query \
25	  --query 'rule.id:${rule_id}' \
26	  --window ${window} \
27	  --run-dir ${run_dir}
28	```
29	
30	For wider windows or noisy rules where match_count likely exceeds
31	`--limit`, pass a JSON search body so the host / srcip / hour
32	distributions come back as server-side true totals instead of a
33	limit-capped sample:
34	
35	```bash
36	python3 soc-agent/scripts/tools/wazuh_cli.py query \
37	  --query '{
38	    "query": {
39	      "bool": {
40	        "must":   [{"query_string": {"query": "rule.id:${rule_id}"}}],
41	        "filter": [{"range": {"timestamp": {"gte": "${start}", "lte": "${end}"}}}]
42	      }
43	    },
44	    "aggs": {
45	      "by_agent":  {"terms": {"field": "agent.name",   "size": 10}},
46	      "by_srcip":  {"terms": {"field": "data.srcip",   "size": 10}},
47	      "by_user":   {"terms": {"field": "data.srcuser", "size": 10}},
48	      "by_hour":   {"date_histogram": {"field": "timestamp", "fixed_interval": "1h"}}
49	    }
50	  }' \
51	  --limit 5 \
52	  --run-dir ${run_dir}
53	```
54	
55	`--limit 5` keeps a handful of recent events for the Sample section;
56	the aggregations carry the totals.
57	
58	## Common pitfalls
59	
60	- Some rules fire every few seconds for healthcheck-style traffic — a
61	  big number is not interesting on its own; look at distribution
62	  across hosts and srcips.
63	- The default Count Breakdown is computed from the post-`--limit`
64	  sample, not the full match set. The CLI labels this when truncated,
65	  but if you need correct totals at scale, use the JSON+aggs form
66	  above.
67

1	---
2	name: defender-wazuh
3	description: Wazuh environment reference for the defender — what data Wazuh holds, the CLI shape, and where the production adapter lives.
4	---
5	
6	Wazuh is the org's primary SIEM. Authentication events, file integrity
7	monitoring, syscall audit, and rule-correlated alerts all surface here.
8	
9	## CLI
10	
11	The defender and gather dispatch Wazuh queries through the production
12	adapter at `soc-agent/scripts/tools/wazuh_cli.py`:
13	
14	```bash
15	python3 soc-agent/scripts/tools/wazuh_cli.py query \
16	  --query '<Lucene>' \
17	  --window 2h \
18	  --run-dir {run_dir}
19	```
20	
21	Common subcommands:
22	
23	- `query` — search the alerts index. `--query` is polymorphic:
24	  - **Lucene string** (`rule.id:5710 AND agent.name:web-03`) — the CLI
25	    wraps it in a bool with the time-range filter from `--start` /
26	    `--end` / `--window`. Best for "show me events" leads.
27	  - **JSON search body** (`'{"query": {...}, "aggs": {...}}'`) — the
28	    agent owns the entire body, including time filtering. Use this
29	    whenever the lead asks for counts, top-N, or distributions over a
30	    population that may exceed `--limit` — server-side aggs return true
31	    totals over the full match set, while the default Count Breakdown
32	    is a post-`--limit` sample.
33	  Other flags: `--limit` (default 500, max 10000; use `0` for
34	  count+aggs only), `--run-dir` (persists raw payload under
35	  `{run_dir}/gather_raw/` and wraps stdout in salted untrusted-data
36	  delimiters), `--raw` (rarely needed; default already embeds first 3
37	  events' `_source`).
38	- `health-check` — connectivity probe; the defender does not need to
39	  invoke this directly during a run.
40	
41	Lucene is OpenSearch query_string syntax: `rule.groups:sshd AND
42	data.srcip:10.0.0.5`. JSON bodies use the standard OpenSearch search
43	DSL — `query.bool.must` / `query.bool.filter`, `aggs.{name}.terms` /
44	`date_histogram` / `cardinality`, etc.
45	
46	Working query examples + field-level pitfalls live with the templates
47	under `defender/skills/gather/queries/wazuh/`. Reach for those when
48	authoring or grepping for a Wazuh measurement; this SKILL covers only
49	the system surface.
50
